Method of Learning
beginner
5 min
The Second Method of Proof: Gradual Ascent from the Quran
Buti introduces the second method, starting with the Quran as a transmitted book.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Buti's second method of proving God's existence, which begins with the Quran as a certain transmitted report and gradually ascends to the truth of God's existence.

Core Idea
The Quran itself is the starting point for a rational ascent to God.

In the previous lesson, Buti presented a direct method of proof. Now he introduces a complementary second method that starts from a tangible, historical reality: the Quran. This method does not abandon rationality but uses the Quran's certain transmission as a scientific fact, then progressively uncovers deeper truths. Let's read how he describes this gradual ascent.

Guided Path
1
Understand the need for a second method
Buti explains that he will not limit himself to the first method but will present a second one. This shows that multiple approaches are valid and complementary.
The second method is not independent but works alongside the first.
2
Grasp the process of gradual ascent
Read how the method starts from a manifest scientific issue, then through analysis reveals further issues, gradually leading to the ultimate truth of God's existence.
Think of this as a chain of reasoning where each step uncovers the next.
3
Apply the method to the Quran
Buti identifies the Quran as the initial manifest issue—a report-based matter. According to scientific method, we investigate its transmission.
This is a key shift: using transmitted knowledge as a starting point for rational proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من أجل هذا لن نقتصر على عرض هذه الطريقة فيما انتهينا إليه ، بل نتجاوزها إلى الطريقة الثانية أيضاً ، وهي الطريقة التي تبدأ بمرحلة الخبر اليقيني ، وهي التي سميناها : طريق التدرج من الادنى وكما قلت لك . فإن هذه الطريقة الثانية تبدأ بالنظر في مسألة علمية ماثلة أمامنا ، حتى إذا انتهينا من تفسيرها ، انكشف لنا من ورائها مسألة أخرى متعلقة بها ، فإذا نظرنا فيها هي ! أيضاً وانتهينا من تحليلها ، انكشفت لنا مسألة عن ثالثة، حتى تتدرج بنا هذه المسائل إلى إثبات الحقيقة ذاتها التي ظهر ثبوتها لنا آنفاً ، وهي حقيقة وجود الله عز وجل نحن الآن أمام كتاب غريب اسمه ( القرآن ( تناقلته إلينا أيدي القرون من مصدر معين ، إذاً فنحن أمام مسألة خبرية تجسدت في صورة هذا الكتاب وعلينا أن نبدأ في تحقيقها حسب المنهج العلمي المتبع للتحقيق في النقول والأخبار . ولدى التحقيق . نعلم بأن هذا الكتاب وصل إلينا ( بسند صحيح متواتر -1.2_
For this reason, we will not confine ourselves to presenting this method as we have done, but will go beyond it to the second method as well, which is the method that begins with the stage of certain report (al-khabar al-yaqini), and which we have called: the way of gradual ascent from the lower. And as I told you, this second method begins by looking at a manifest scientific issue before us. When we finish interpreting it, another related issue is revealed to us from behind it. Then if we look into it as well and finish analyzing it, a third issue is revealed to us, until these issues gradually lead us to the proof of the very truth whose certainty appeared to us earlier, namely the truth of the existence of God Almighty. We are now before a strange book called the Quran, which the hands of centuries have transmitted to us from a specific source. So we are before a report-based issue (mas'ala khabariyya) embodied in the form of this book. We must begin to investigate it according to the scientific method followed for investigating transmissions and reports. Upon investigation, we know that this book has reached us with a sound, mutawatir chain of transmission -1.2_
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage introduces the second method of proof for God's existence: the way of gradual ascent from the lower. It starts with a manifest scientific issue, such as the Quran as a transmitted book. By analyzing this issue, related questions are uncovered, and gradually the truth of God's existence is reached. The author identifies the Quran as a report-based issue and states that it should be investigated using the scientific method for examining transmissions. The outcome is that the Quran has reached us with a sound, mutawatir chain of transmission, establishing its credibility.

Key Terms
الخبر اليقيني
طريق التدرج
المسألة الخبرية
المنهج العلمي
السند الصحيح
المتواتر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the second method is independent of the first.
Correction: The second method is complementary, starting from a different point but leading to the same truth.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, what is the starting point of the second method of proof?
A) The existence of God.
B) A manifest scientific issue, like the Quran.
C) Rational premises.
D) The fabrication of doubts.

Key Takeaway
The second method begins with the certain transmission of the Quran and gradually ascends to prove God's existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You are now before the Quran as a transmitted book. Have you ever personally investigated its chain of transmission to verify its authenticity? What is holding you back from this step of certainty?
?
The method begins with a manifest issue. What is the most 'manifest' issue in your life right now that, if followed, could lead you to a deeper truth about God? Will you follow it?
?
If the Quran is mutawatir and certain, why do you sometimes live as if it were not? What would change today if you truly acted on the certainty this method claims to establish?

Method of Learning
beginner
4 min
Introduction to the Path of Gradual Ascent
Buti introduces the second method and its step-by-step progression.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the overall structure of the second method (tariq al-tadarruj) and its starting point as a chain of questions leading to God.

Core Idea
The second method climbs from a tangible fact to God through linked questions.

Buti now presents a second method that does not start abstractly but from a concrete, transmitted fact—the Qur'an. This method gradually ascends through a series of connected questions, each leading to the next, until the truth of God's existence is reached. The passage outlines the general approach before diving into specifics.

Guided Path
1
Understand the method's name and logic
The term 'gradual ascent from the lowest' means starting from something accessible and moving upward. Here 'lowest' refers to a well-known report (the Qur'an).
This is a methodological choice to begin with something that is widely accepted.
2
Notice the chain of questions
Buti describes a process: a scientific question leads to another related question, then another, until the final truth emerges. Try to visualize this as a staircase.
3
Identify the endpoint
The ultimate goal is proving the truth of God's existence, which the first method already established. This method provides a different route to the same conclusion.
Buti assumes the existence of God is already known from the first method; this is a complementary approach.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من أجل هذا لن نقتصر على عرض هذه الطريقة فيما انتهينا إليه، بل نتجاوزها إلى الطريقة الثانية أيضاً، وهي الطريقة التي تبدأ بمرحلة الخبر اليقيني، والتي سميناها: طريق التدرج من الأدنى. وكما قلت لك، فإن هذه الطريقة الثانية تبدأ بالنظر في مسألة علمية ماثلة أمامنا، حتى إذا انتهينا من تفسيرها، انكشف لنا من ورائها مسألة أخرى متعلقة بها، فإذا نظرنا فيها هي أيضاً وانتهينا من تحليلها، انكشفت لنا مسألة عن ثالثة، حتى تتدرج بنا هذه المسائل إلى إثبات الحقيقة ذاتها التي ظهر ثبوتها لنا آنفاً، وهي حقيقة وجود الله عز وجل. نحن الآن أمام كتاب غريب اسمه (القرآن) تناقلته إلينا أيدي القرون من مصدر معين، إذاً فنحن أمام مسألة خبرية تجسدت في صورة هذا الكتاب، وعلينا أن نبدأ في تحقيقها حسب المنهج العلمي المتبع للتحقيق في النقول والأخبار. ولدى التحقيق، نعلم بأن هذا الكتاب وصل إلينا (بسند صحيح متواتر لا يخضع لإمكان الكذب في روايته) عن رجل اسمه محمد بن عبد الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ظهر في غضون القرن السادس الميلادي في الجزيرة العربية. كما نعلم لدى التحقيق في ذلك أيضاً بأن الرواية الصحيحة المتواترة أثبتت أنه كان يقول بأن هذا الكتاب ليس تأليفه وليس له كسب في شيء منه، وإنما هو يتلقاه وحياً من الله بواسطة من جبريل عليه السلام. فإذا انتهينا من تحقيق كل من هذين الخبرين، وجدنا أنفسنا أمام مسألة علمية أخرى هي ظاهرة هذا الوحي الذي أخبر عنه محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم فما هي حقيقته؟ وما الفرق بينه وبين الإلهام النفسي؟ وما مدى الاحتمالات العقلية للكذب في هذه الدعوى؟ فهذه قضية علمية أخرى ليست نقلاً حتى يكون تحقيقه عن طريق الرواية والسند، وليست حقيقة مادية محسوسة حتى يكون تحقيقها عن طريق التجربة المحسوسة المشاهدة، وإنما هي من قبيل القضايا العقلية المجردة، فليس من سبيل للتحقيق في أمرها إلا سبيل برهاني اللزوم البين والقياس اليقيني الأولى القائمين على الاستقراء التام. ونحن عندما نحقق في (ظاهرة الوحي) على هذا الأساس، نضطر إلى القطع بأن الوحي لم يكن شعوراً داخلياً ساور محمداً عليه الصلاة والسلام، وبأنه لم يكذب على الناس فيما قال، وبأن أحداً ممن كان في عصره لم يكن يختبئ خلفه ليعلمه هذا الذي يقول عنه إنه وحي من الله، وبأنه لا يمكن أن يكون وسوسة جن أو شياطين؛ نضطر إلى القطع بنفي هذه الاحتمالات بدليل التلازم والقياس الأولى والاستقراء الدقيق التام. وأنت تعلم أن المكان الملائم لتفصيل هذه البراهين وعرضها عند البحث في قسم النبوات الآتي قريباً إن شاء الله، وإنما نحن هنا نصور خطوات البحث ومراحله وكيفية التدرج من الأدنى إلى النهاية التي سنكتشفها. فإذا انتهينا من التحقيق في الوحي بهذا الشكل، وجدنا أنفسنا أمام ضرورة
For this reason we will not restrict ourselves to presenting this method in what we have concluded, but we will go beyond it to the second method as well, which is the method that begins with the stage of certain report (al-khabar al-yaqini), which we called: the path of gradual ascent from the lowest (tariq al-tadarruj min al-adna). And as I told you, this second method begins by looking into a present scientific question before us, until when we finish explaining it, another question related to it is revealed to us from behind it. Then if we look into it as well and finish analyzing it, a third question is revealed to us, until these questions gradually advance us to proving the very truth that has already appeared to us, which is the truth of the existence of God Almighty. We are now before a strange book called (the Qur'an) which the hands of centuries have transmitted to us from a specific source. So we are before a matter of report (mas'ala khabariyya) embodied in the form of this book, and we must begin to investigate it according to the scientific methodology followed for investigating transmitted reports and news. Upon investigation, we know that this book reached us (with a sound, mutawatir chain that is not subject to the possibility of lying in its transmission) from a man named Muhammad ibn Abdullah, may God bless him and grant him peace, who appeared during the sixth century CE in the Arabian Peninsula. We also know from investigation that the sound, mutawatir report also established that he used to say that this book is not his authorship and he has no acquisition in any part of it, but rather he receives it as revelation (wahy) from God through the agency of Gabriel, peace be upon him. When we finish investigating both of these reports, we find ourselves before another scientific question, which is the phenomenon of this revelation that Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, informed about. So what is its reality? What is the difference between it and psychological inspiration (al-ilham al-nafsi)? What are the extent of the rational possibilities of lying in this claim? This is another scientific issue that is not a transmission so that its investigation be through narration and chain, nor is it a material sensed reality so that its investigation be through sensed observed experiment, but rather it is of the kind of abstract rational issues (al-qadaya al-'aqliyya al-mujarrada). So there is no way to investigate its matter except through the demonstrative way of clear implication (burhan al-luzum al-bayyin) and the primary certain syllogism (al-qiyas al-yaqini al-awwali) based on complete induction (al-istiqra' al-tamm). And when we investigate (the phenomenon of revelation) on this basis, we are compelled to conclude that the revelation was not an internal feeling that occurred to Muhammad, peace and blessings be upon him, and that he did not lie to people in what he said, and that no one from his era was hiding behind him to teach him this which he says is revelation from God, and that it cannot be the whispering of a jinn or devils. We are compelled to negate these possibilities by the proof of implication (dalil al-talazum), primary syllogism, and precise complete induction. And you know that the appropriate place for detailing these proofs and presenting them is in the upcoming section on prophethood, God willing. And here we are only depicting the steps of research and its stages and how to gradually ascend from the lowest to the end that we will discover. And when we finish investigating revelation in this way, we find ourselves before a necessity...
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage introduces the second method of proving God's existence: the path of gradual ascent from the lowest (tariq al-tadarruj min al-adna). Buti explains that unlike the first method (not detailed here), this second method starts from a certain report (khabar yaqini)—specifically the Qur'an. It begins by examining a tangible 'scientific question' (here the Qur'an as a transmitted book) and then proceeds from one question to another, each related to the previous, until it reaches the ultimate truth of God's existence. The method is described as a chain: first, investigate the Qur'an as a historical report; second, investigate its claimed source (revelation); third, use rational proofs to determine the true nature of revelation; and finally, the conclusion that revelation is truly from God, thus establishing His existence. Buti emphasizes the methodological shift: the first question (the Qur'an) is a matter of transmission (khabar), investigated by chains of narration. Upon confirming that it comes with a sound, mutawatir chain from Muhammad (PBUH) who claimed it is revelation, we then face a second question: the reality of revelation itself. This is not a matter of transmission or empirical observation, but a rational issue. Therefore, it requires demonstrative proofs such as the proof of clear implication (burhan al-luzum al-bayyin), primary certain syllogism (al-qiyas al-yaqini al-awwali), and complete induction (al-istiqra' al-tamm). Using these, we can rule out all alternative explanations (internal feeling, lying, human teaching, demonic whispers) and conclude that revelation is true, leading to the necessity of God's existence. Buti notes that detailed proofs will be given in the later section on prophethood, so here he only outlines the steps.

Key Terms
طريق التدرج من الأدنى
الخبر اليقيني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the starting point of the second method according to Buti?
A) Rational arguments for the necessity of a creator
B) The empirical observation of natural phenomena
C) The stage of certain report (al-khabar al-yaqini)
D) Direct intuition of the divine

Key Takeaway
The second method starts from a certain, transmitted fact and progresses through linked questions to prove God's existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever experienced a chain of questions in your own life that led you to a deeper certainty about God? What was that starting question?
?
Buti describes a method that begins with a 'certain report'—the Qur'an. Do you treat the Qur'an as such a certain starting point in your daily life, or do you often begin with your own doubts? What would change if you truly started from that certainty?
?
This method requires patience to move through linked questions. In your spiritual journey, are you willing to follow such a patient, step-by-step path, or do you expect immediate answers? What is holding you back from taking the first step?

Method of Learning
beginner
4 min
Investigating the Qur'an as a Certain Report
Buti investigates the Qur'an as a historical report and extracts two certain conclusions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Qur'an is investigated as a historical report and what the investigation reveals about its transmission and claimed source.

Core Idea
The Qur'an reaches us through an unbroken chain that precludes lies.

After introducing the method, Buti now applies it to the first concrete question: the Qur'an itself. He treats it as a transmitted report that must be verified according to scientific methods of historical investigation. The passage shows how this verification leads to two key facts: the Qur'an's sound transmission from Muhammad (PBUH) and Muhammad's claim that it is divine revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the two findings
The passage presents two results of investigating the Qur'an: (1) it reached us via a sound mutawatir chain from Muhammad, and (2) Muhammad said it is revelation from God. Note how each is established.
The investigation uses the methodology of verifying transmissions (riwaya) and chains (sanad).
2
Understand the significance of 'mutawatir'
'Mutawatir' means reported by so many people at every level that it is impossible for them to have conspired to lie. This gives certainty.
3
Notice the shift from book to claim
Once we have the book as a fact, we move to the next question: the claim of revelation. This is a new issue that requires a different type of investigation.
This sets up the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من أجل هذا لن نقتصر على عرض هذه الطريقة فيما انتهينا إليه، بل نتجاوزها إلى الطريقة الثانية أيضاً، وهي الطريقة التي تبدأ بمرحلة الخبر اليقيني، والتي سميناها: طريق التدرج من الأدنى. وكما قلت لك، فإن هذه الطريقة الثانية تبدأ بالنظر في مسألة علمية ماثلة أمامنا، حتى إذا انتهينا من تفسيرها، انكشف لنا من ورائها مسألة أخرى متعلقة بها، فإذا نظرنا فيها هي أيضاً وانتهينا من تحليلها، انكشفت لنا مسألة عن ثالثة، حتى تتدرج بنا هذه المسائل إلى إثبات الحقيقة ذاتها التي ظهر ثبوتها لنا آنفاً، وهي حقيقة وجود الله عز وجل. نحن الآن أمام كتاب غريب اسمه (القرآن) تناقلته إلينا أيدي القرون من مصدر معين، إذاً فنحن أمام مسألة خبرية تجسدت في صورة هذا الكتاب، وعلينا أن نبدأ في تحقيقها حسب المنهج العلمي المتبع للتحقيق في النقول والأخبار. ولدى التحقيق، نعلم بأن هذا الكتاب وصل إلينا (بسند صحيح متواتر لا يخضع لإمكان الكذب في روايته) عن رجل اسمه محمد بن عبد الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ظهر في غضون القرن السادس الميلادي في الجزيرة العربية. كما نعلم لدى التحقيق في ذلك أيضاً بأن الرواية الصحيحة المتواترة أثبتت أنه كان يقول بأن هذا الكتاب ليس تأليفه وليس له كسب في شيء منه، وإنما هو يتلقاه وحياً من الله بواسطة من جبريل عليه السلام. فإذا انتهينا من تحقيق كل من هذين الخبرين، وجدنا أنفسنا أمام مسألة علمية أخرى هي ظاهرة هذا الوحي الذي أخبر عنه محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم فما هي حقيقته؟ وما الفرق بينه وبين الإلهام النفسي؟ وما مدى الاحتمالات العقلية للكذب في هذه الدعوى؟ فهذه قضية علمية أخرى ليست نقلاً حتى يكون تحقيقه عن طريق الرواية والسند، وليست حقيقة مادية محسوسة حتى يكون تحقيقها عن طريق التجربة المحسوسة المشاهدة، وإنما هي من قبيل القضايا العقلية المجردة، فليس من سبيل للتحقيق في أمرها إلا سبيل برهاني اللزوم البين والقياس اليقيني الأولى القائمين على الاستقراء التام. ونحن عندما نحقق في (ظاهرة الوحي) على هذا الأساس، نضطر إلى القطع بأن الوحي لم يكن شعوراً داخلياً ساور محمداً عليه الصلاة والسلام، وبأنه لم يكذب على الناس فيما قال، وبأن أحداً ممن كان في عصره لم يكن يختبئ خلفه ليعلمه هذا الذي يقول عنه إنه وحي من الله، وبأنه لا يمكن أن يكون وسوسة جن أو شياطين؛ نضطر إلى القطع بنفي هذه الاحتمالات بدليل التلازم والقياس الأولى والاستقراء الدقيق التام. وأنت تعلم أن المكان الملائم لتفصيل هذه البراهين وعرضها عند البحث في قسم النبوات الآتي قريباً إن شاء الله، وإنما نحن هنا نصور خطوات البحث ومراحله وكيفية التدرج من الأدنى إلى النهاية التي سنكتشفها. فإذا انتهينا من التحقيق في الوحي بهذا الشكل، وجدنا أنفسنا أمام ضرورة
For this reason we will not restrict ourselves to presenting this method in what we have concluded, but we will go beyond it to the second method as well, which is the method that begins with the stage of certain report (al-khabar al-yaqini), which we called: the path of gradual ascent from the lowest (tariq al-tadarruj min al-adna). And as I told you, this second method begins by looking into a present scientific question before us, until when we finish explaining it, another question related to it is revealed to us from behind it. Then if we look into it as well and finish analyzing it, a third question is revealed to us, until these questions gradually advance us to proving the very truth that has already appeared to us, which is the truth of the existence of God Almighty. We are now before a strange book called (the Qur'an) which the hands of centuries have transmitted to us from a specific source. So we are before a matter of report (mas'ala khabariyya) embodied in the form of this book, and we must begin to investigate it according to the scientific methodology followed for investigating transmitted reports and news. Upon investigation, we know that this book reached us (with a sound, mutawatir chain that is not subject to the possibility of lying in its transmission) from a man named Muhammad ibn Abdullah, may God bless him and grant him peace, who appeared during the sixth century CE in the Arabian Peninsula. We also know from investigation that the sound, mutawatir report also established that he used to say that this book is not his authorship and he has no acquisition in any part of it, but rather he receives it as revelation (wahy) from God through the agency of Gabriel, peace be upon him. When we finish investigating both of these reports, we find ourselves before another scientific question, which is the phenomenon of this revelation that Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, informed about. So what is its reality? What is the difference between it and psychological inspiration (al-ilham al-nafsi)? What are the extent of the rational possibilities of lying in this claim? This is another scientific issue that is not a transmission so that its investigation be through narration and chain, nor is it a material sensed reality so that its investigation be through sensed observed experiment, but rather it is of the kind of abstract rational issues (al-qadaya al-'aqliyya al-mujarrada). So there is no way to investigate its matter except through the demonstrative way of clear implication (burhan al-luzum al-bayyin) and the primary certain syllogism (al-qiyas al-yaqini al-awwali) based on complete induction (al-istiqra' al-tamm). And when we investigate (the phenomenon of revelation) on this basis, we are compelled to conclude that the revelation was not an internal feeling that occurred to Muhammad, peace and blessings be upon him, and that he did not lie to people in what he said, and that no one from his era was hiding behind him to teach him this which he says is revelation from God, and that it cannot be the whispering of a jinn or devils. We are compelled to negate these possibilities by the proof of implication (dalil al-talazum), primary syllogism, and precise complete induction. And you know that the appropriate place for detailing these proofs and presenting them is in the upcoming section on prophethood, God willing. And here we are only depicting the steps of research and its stages and how to gradually ascend from the lowest to the end that we will discover. And when we finish investigating revelation in this way, we find ourselves before a necessity...
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage introduces the second method of proving God's existence: the path of gradual ascent from the lowest (tariq al-tadarruj min al-adna). Buti explains that unlike the first method (not detailed here), this second method starts from a certain report (khabar yaqini)—specifically the Qur'an. It begins by examining a tangible 'scientific question' (here the Qur'an as a transmitted book) and then proceeds from one question to another, each related to the previous, until it reaches the ultimate truth of God's existence. The method is described as a chain: first, investigate the Qur'an as a historical report; second, investigate its claimed source (revelation); third, use rational proofs to determine the true nature of revelation; and finally, the conclusion that revelation is truly from God, thus establishing His existence. Buti emphasizes the methodological shift: the first question (the Qur'an) is a matter of transmission (khabar), investigated by chains of narration. Upon confirming that it comes with a sound, mutawatir chain from Muhammad (PBUH) who claimed it is revelation, we then face a second question: the reality of revelation itself. This is not a matter of transmission or empirical observation, but a rational issue. Therefore, it requires demonstrative proofs such as the proof of clear implication (burhan al-luzum al-bayyin), primary certain syllogism (al-qiyas al-yaqini al-awwali), and complete induction (al-istiqra' al-tamm). Using these, we can rule out all alternative explanations (internal feeling, lying, human teaching, demonic whispers) and conclude that revelation is true, leading to the necessity of God's existence. Buti notes that detailed proofs will be given in the later section on prophethood, so here he only outlines the steps.

Key Terms
الخبر اليقيني
السند الصحيح المتواتر
الوحي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) It is a collection of pre-Islamic poetry

Key Takeaway
The Qur'an is a certain historical report that also transmits Muhammad's claim of divine revelation.

?
The investigation of the Qur'an as a report gives you certainty about its authenticity. What step can you take right now to move from knowing this intellectually to feeling it in your heart and letting it transform your daily actions?

Revelation as a Rational Issue: Proofs and Certainty
Buti argues that revelation must be investigated rationally and uses proofs to rule out all alternative explanations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the phenomenon of revelation is a rational issue and how demonstrative proofs (clear implication, primary syllogism, complete induction) eliminate all alternative explanations, compelling the conclusion that revelation is true.

Core Idea
Revelation is proven true by eliminating all other rational possibilities.

Having established that Muhammad claimed revelation, Buti now shifts from historical investigation to rational analysis. The phenomenon of revelation cannot be verified by chains of transmission or empirical observation; it requires abstract reasoning. Buti outlines the proofs that will be detailed later, showing how they rule out every possible alternative—internal feeling, lying, human tutoring, or demonic influence—leaving only the truth of divine revelation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nature of the new question
Buti says revelation is not a transmission (naql) nor a material sensation, but a rational issue (qadiyya 'aqliyya). This determines the method of investigation.
2
List the alternative explanations
The passage enumerates four possibilities that must be negated: internal feeling, lying, a hidden human teacher, and jinn/devil whispering. Each is eliminated by rational proofs.
These are the only logical alternatives to genuine revelation.
3
Understand the proofs used
Buti mentions three types of proofs: burhan al-luzum al-bayyin (clear implication), al-qiyas al-yaqini al-awwali (primary certain syllogism), and al-istiqra' al-tamm (complete induction). These are demonstrated through analysis of Muhammad's life and the Qur'an.
Detailed proofs are promised in the later section on prophethood.
4
Note the conclusion
After eliminating alternatives, we are compelled to accept that revelation is true, which leads to the necessity of God's existence (though the passage cuts off).
This is the second step of the gradual ascent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

الطريقة الثانية تبدأ بالنظر في مسألة علمية ماثلة أمامنا، حتى إذا انتهينا من تفسيرها، انكشف لنا من ورائها مسألة أخرى متعلقة بها، فإذا نظرنا فيها هي أيضاً وانتهينا من تحليلها، انكشفت لنا مسألة عن ثالثة، حتى تتدرج بنا هذه المسائل إلى إثبات الحقيقة ذاتها التي ظهر ثبوتها لنا آنفاً، وهي حقيقة وجود الله عز وجل. نحن الآن أمام كتاب غريب اسمه (القرآن) تناقلته إلينا أيدي القرون من مصدر معين، إذاً فنحن أمام هذا الكتاب ليس تأليفه وليس له كسب في شيء منه، وإنما هو يتلقاه وحياً من الله بواسطة من جبريل عليه السلام. فإذا انتهينا من تحقيق كل من هذين الخبرين، وجدنا أنفسنا أمام مسألة علمية أخرى هي ظاهرة هذا الوحي الذي أخبر عنه محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم فما هي حقيقته؟ وما الفرق بينه وبين الإلهام النفسي؟ وما مدى الاحتمالات العقلية للكذب في هذه الدعوى؟ فهذه قضية علمية أخرى ليست نقلاً حتى يكون تحقيقه عن طريق الرواية والسند، وليست حقيقة مادية محسوسة حتى يكون تحقيقها عن طريق التجربة المحسوسة المشاهدة، وإنما هي من قبيل القضايا العقلية المجردة، فليس من سبيل للتحقيق في أمرها إلا سبيل برهاني اللزوم البين والقياس اليقيني الأولى القائمين على الاستقراء التام. ونحن عندما نحقق في (ظاهرة الوحي) على هذا الأساس، نضطر إلى القطع بأن الوحي لم يكن شعوراً داخلياً ساور محمداً عليه الصلاة والسلام، وبأنه لم يكذب على الناس فيما قال، وبأن أحداً ممن كان في عصره لم يكن يختبئ خلفه ليعلمه هذا الذي يقول عنه إنه وحي من الله، وبأنه لا يمكن أن يكون وسوسة جن أو شياطين؛ نضطر إلى القطع بنفي هذه الاحتمالات بدليل التلازم والقياس إلى النهاية التي سنكتشفها. فإذا انتهينا من التحقيق في الوحي بهذا الشكل، وجدنا أنفسنا أمام ضرورة
For this reason we will not restrict ourselves to presenting this method in what we have concluded, but we will go beyond it to the second method as well, which is the method that begins with the stage of certain report (al-khabar al-yaqini), which we called: the path of gradual ascent from the lowest (tariq al-tadarruj min al-adna). And as I told you, this second method begins by looking into a present scientific question before us, until when we finish explaining it, another question related to it is revealed to us from behind it. Then if we look into it as well and finish analyzing it, a third question is revealed to us, until these questions gradually advance us to proving the very truth that has already appeared to us, which is the truth of the existence of God Almighty. We are now before a strange book called (the Qur'an) which the hands of centuries have transmitted to us from a specific source. Upon investigation, we know that this book reached us (with a sound, mutawatir chain that is not subject to the possibility of lying in its transmission) from a man named Muhammad ibn Abdullah, may God bless him and grant him peace, who appeared during the sixth century CE in the Arabian Peninsula. We also know from investigation that the sound, mutawatir report also established that he used to say that this book is not his authorship and he has no acquisition in any part of it, but rather he receives it as revelation (wahy) from God through the agency of Gabriel, peace be upon him. And here we are only depicting the steps of research and its stages and how to gradually ascend from the lowest to the end that we will discover. And when we finish investigating revelation in this way, we find ourselves before a necessity...

From Historical Reports to Rational Investigation of Revelation
Buti describes how investigating the Quran and the messenger raises the question of revelation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the verified reports about the Prophet Muhammad and the Quran lead to a rational investigation of the nature of revelation, distinct from historical or empirical inquiry.

Core Idea
The reliability of the Quran and the Prophet's claim forces a rational investigation into revelation.

Buti has just shown that the two reports—the historical account of Muhammad and the textual transmission of the Quran—are so reliable that falsehood is impossible. Now he takes the next step: the Prophet himself claimed the Quran is revelation. This claim raises a new question that cannot be answered by history or science alone. It demands a rational inquiry into what revelation truly is.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the two reliable reports
Begin by noting that Buti refers to two reports: one about the person of Muhammad (peace be upon him) and one about the Quran being revealed. Both are established as authentic and beyond doubt.
This sets the foundation: we are building on certain knowledge.
2
Identify the Prophet's claim
The Prophet stated that the Quran is not his own work but revelation from Allah through Jibril. This claim is part of the second report and is itself reliable.
The claim is not a separate speculation; it's transmitted as fact.
3
Understand the nature of the new question
Buti explains that investigating the phenomenon of revelation is different from verifying historical or physical facts. It is a rational issue, not a matter of narration or experiment.
This shifts the methodology from textual criticism to rational proof.
4
Learn the correct method for rational inquiry
The method for such a rational issue is 'clear entailment' (al-luzum al-bayyin) and 'certain primary analogical reasoning' (al-qiyas al-yaqini al-awwali) based on complete induction.
This prepares the reader for the upcoming argumentation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا يخضع لإمكان الكذب في روايته عن رجل اسمه محمد بن عبد الله ما ظهر في غضون القرن السادس الميلادي في الجزيرة العربية. كما نعلم لدى التحقيق في ذلك أيضاً بأن الرواية الصحيحة المتواترة أثبتت أنه كان يقول بأن هذا الكتاب ليس تأليفه وليس له كسب في شيء منه، وإنما هو يتلقاه وحياً من الله بواسطة من جبريل عليه السلام!.. فإذا انتهينا من تحقيق كل من هذين الخبرين، وجدنا أنفسنا أمام مسألة علمية أخرى هي ظاهرة هذا الوحي الذي أخبر عنه محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم فما هي حقيقته؟ وما الفرق بينه وبين الإلهام النفسي؟ وما مدى الاحتمالات العقلية للكذب في هذه الدعوى؟ فهذه قضية علمية أخرى ليست نقلاً حتى يكون تحقيقه عن طريق الرواية والسند، وليست حقيقة مادية محسوسة حتى يكون تحقيقها عن طريق التجربة المحسوسة المشاهدة، وإنما هي من قبيل القضايا العقلية المجردة، فليس من سبيل للتحقيق في أمرها إلا سبيل برهاني اللزوم البين والقياس اليقيني الأولى القائمين على الاستقراء التام.
It is not subject to the possibility of falsehood in its narration about a man named Muhammad ibn Abdullah who appeared during the sixth century CE in Arabia. And we also know, through investigation of that, that the authentic mutawatir narration proved that he used to say that this book is not his authorship and he has no earning in anything of it, but rather he receives it as revelation from Allah through the intermediary of Jibril (peace be upon him). So when we complete the investigation of each of these two reports, we find ourselves before another scientific issue, which is the phenomenon of this revelation that Muhammad (peace and blessings be upon him) reported. So what is its reality? And what is the difference between it and psychological inspiration? And what is the extent of the rational possibilities of falsehood in this claim? So this is another scientific issue that is not a transmitted report so that its verification would be through narration and chain, nor is it a material sensible reality so that its verification would be through sensory observed experiment, but rather it is of the type of abstract rational issues. So there is no way to investigate it except through the demonstrative path of clear entailment and certain primary analogical reasoning based on complete induction.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage establishes the groundwork for a rational investigation of prophetic revelation. Buti begins by noting that the report about Muhammad is so reliable that it cannot be subject to falsehood. Investigation shows that the Quran is claimed to be revelation. This leads to the core question: what is revelation? Buti classifies this as a rational issue, not a historical or empirical one. Therefore, it must be studied through logical deduction, entailment, and induction.

Certainty in Premises Requires Certainty in Conclusion
Buti states the logical necessity of certainty in conclusion from certain premises.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why certainty in premises logically compels certainty in conclusion, and why doubting the conclusion while certain of the premises would be a contradiction.

Core Idea
Certainty in premises leaves no room for doubt in the conclusion.

This short but powerful passage from Buti establishes a fundamental logical principle: if you are truly certain of your premises, you must also be certain of the conclusion. To think otherwise would be to accept a contradiction. This principle is the bedrock of his argument that rational inquiry leads to certainty about God.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Let the logical flow of Buti's argument sink in.
Notice the concise style of the argument.
2
Identify the logical structure
Buti presents a condition (certain premises) and a necessary result (certainty in conclusion). Identify the 'if...then' logic.
3
Understand the contradiction
Reflect on why doubting the conclusion while certain of the premises would be like affirming two opposites at once. Why is that impossible?
This connects to the law of non-contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذلك أن إدراك المقدمات اليقينية بشروطها العلمية المعروفة، يفرض على المدرك الإيمان بنتيجتها، إذ لا يتصور الشك في النتيجة مع الإيمان اليقيني بالمقدمة. ولو جاز تصور ذلك، لجاز تصور اجتماع النقيضين في مكان واحد وزمان واحد.
That is because the perception of certain premises with their known scientific conditions imposes upon the perceiver belief in their conclusion, for it is inconceivable to doubt the conclusion while having certain belief in the premise. And if that were conceivable, then the combination of two contradictories in one place and one time would be conceivable.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage is a logical principle. Buti states that if one fully understands certain premises under proper conditions, one is compelled to accept the conclusion. To doubt the conclusion while being certain of the premises would be a contradiction, comparable to affirming two opposites simultaneously. This supports his argument that the researcher who follows the rational path to God must end up with certainty.

Key Terms
المقدمات اليقينية (certain premises)
النتيجة (conclusion)
النقيضين (two contradictories)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: It is possible to be certain of premises yet doubt the conclusion because one might not see the connection.
Correction: Buti argues that this would be a logical contradiction, equivalent to affirming two opposites simultaneously.

Checkpoint
What logical impossibility would follow if someone doubted a conclusion while being certain of its premises?
A) An infinite regress
B) The combination of two contradictories
C) Circular reasoning
D) A false analogy

Key Takeaway
Certainty in premises logically necessitates certainty in conclusion, otherwise a contradiction arises.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you certain that Allah exists, that the Quran is His word, and that you will be accountable for your deeds? If so, then why do you sometimes act as if these conclusions are doubtful? This lesson says certainty in premises demands certainty in conclusion—so what is missing in your premises or your reasoning?
?
When you are absolutely certain of a truth from revelation, yet you find yourself hesitating to live by it, are you not harboring a contradiction? Buti's logical principle exposes that such hesitation is impossible if you are truly certain. Will you today re-examine what you claim to be certain of, and purge the doubt from your heart?
?
Imagine you are standing before Allah and He asks you: 'Were you certain of My signs, or were you merely assuming?' Based on this lesson, your doubt about any fundamental belief would indicate a lack of true certainty in the premises. What step will you take today to move from half-hearted acceptance to genuine certainty?

Certainty Upon Certainty: The Cumulative Power of Rational Proofs
Buti explains that other rational proofs provide certainty upon certainty for the believer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why multiple rational proofs, when combined with revelation, produce an unshakeable certainty that no doubt can penetrate.

Core Idea
Multiple proofs yield certainty upon certainty, forming an impenetrable fortress of belief.

Buti has already established that revelation provides certainty. Now he explains that additional rational proofs, far from being redundant, add layer upon layer of certainty. The combination creates a methodology so robust that no doubt can even approach it. This passage highlights the cumulative epistemic strength of multiple lines of evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the translation. Let the author's words sink in before interpreting.
2
Understand 'certainty upon certainty'
Identify what Buti means by 'يقيناً فوق يقين'. How does this differ from a single certainty? Consider why multiple proofs are not redundant.
Buti uses a superlative structure to stress accumulation.
3
Reflect on the methodology
Examine the phrase 'منهج علمي لا يمكن أن يدنو إليه أي ريبة أو شك'. What does this say about the nature of Islamic theology? How does it protect the believer's faith?
This shows the integration of revealed and rational evidence.
4
Apply the insight
Write down why this cumulative certainty is important for your own faith. How does it strengthen conviction?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غير أن الباحث عندما يصل إلى النتيجة القطعية التي تفرض عليه الإيمان بالله، يجد هناك تلك البراهين العقلية الأخرى قائمة أمام ذهنه فيكسبه ذلك يقيناً فوق يقين، ويتحقق له من كلا الطريقتين منهج علمي لا يمكن أن يدنو إليه أو يطوف حوله أي ريبة أو شك.
However, when the researcher reaches the decisive conclusion that imposes upon him belief in God, he finds there those other rational proofs standing before his mind, and that gives him certainty upon certainty, and there is realized for him from both methods a scientific methodology that no doubt or suspicion can approach or circle around.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
Buti notes that even after reaching certainty through one path (the path from revelation), additional rational proofs (the first method discussed earlier) reinforce that certainty, producing 'certainty upon certainty'. The combination of both methods yields a methodology immune to any doubt or suspicion. This emphasizes the cumulative epistemic strength of multiple arguments.

Correction: Buti explains that multiple proofs produce 'certainty upon certainty', strengthening faith and creating a methodology immune to doubt. Additional rational proofs are not redundant but cumulative.

?

Warning Against Reading Extravagant Sufi Books
Buti advises prohibition of reading certain Sufi books without declaring takfir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Buti's nuanced position on reading books with shatahat: they are prohibited to read, but one must not engage in takfir of the author.

Core Idea
Avoid the books, not the author.

Buti concludes his discussion on negative attributes by emphasizing sufficiency of the given knowledge. He then turns to a practical methodological advice: while we must avoid reading books that contain extravagant utterances (shatahat), such as al-Futuhat al-Makkiyya and Fusus al-Hikam, we must not fall into the error of declaring their author an unbeliever. This passage teaches a balanced approach to problematic texts.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic original and English translation to grasp Buti's precise wording.
2
Identify the two parts of Buti's advice
Notice that Buti gives a positive statement (this suffices) and then a specific caution. Distinguish between the prohibition of reading and the prohibition of takfir.
3
Understand 'shatahat' and the named books
The term 'shatahat' refers to ecstatic utterances that may seem unorthodox. Buti names two famous works by Ibn Arabi as examples.
Shatahat are not necessarily heretical; they require careful interpretation.
4
Reflect on the balance
Buti's approach avoids two extremes: uncritical acceptance and harsh condemnation. This reflects a mature methodology.
This connects to broader principles of dealing with ambiguous texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فهذا يكفيك في أداء أمانة العلم والدين ويكفي الناس في التنبه إلى الحق، وما كلفك الله بأكثر من ذلك. وليسعك ما وسع أئمتنا الأعلام من قبل، من بيان حرمة قراءة هذه الكتب التي تتحدت عن مثل هذه الشطحات كالفتوحات المكية وفصوص الحكم للشيخ محي الدين، وأن على الناس أن يتجنبوها، دون أن تقتحم إلى تكفير بعينه
This suffices you in fulfilling the trust of knowledge and religion, and suffices the people in awakening to the truth, and God has not obligated you with more than that. And let what our eminent imams before you sufficed suffice you, regarding the declaration of the prohibition of reading these books that speak about such extravagant utterances, like al-Futuhat al-Makkiyya and Fusus al-Hikam of Shaykh Muhyi al-Din, and that the people must avoid them, without you delving into declaring a specific person an unbeliever.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage is an editorial caution by Buti. He states that the preceding explanation (likely on negative attributes) is sufficient for fulfilling the trust of knowledge and religion, and one should not go beyond it. He then advises that the reader should be content with the stance of earlier eminent imams who declared the prohibition of reading certain books, namely al-Futuhat al-Makkiyya and Fusus al-Hikam by Muhyi al-Din Ibn Arabi, which contain 'shatahat' (extravagant utterances). However, he warns against going as far as declaring a specific person an unbeliever (takfir). This reflects a nuanced approach of avoiding problematic works without engaging in personal condemnation.

Key Terms
حرمة القراءة
الشطحات
الفتوحات المكية
فصوص الحكم
تكفير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Buti is calling for outright condemnation of Ibn Arabi
Correction: Buti warns against reading his books without declaring him an unbeliever.

Checkpoint

A) They must be read with caution
B) They are prohibited to read, but one should not declare takfir of the author
C) They are recommended
D) They are only for scholars

Key Takeaway
Buti teaches that books containing shatahat should be avoided, but their author should not be declared an unbeliever.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Importance and Method of Studying Divine Attributes
Buti states the importance of divine attributes and outlines his explanatory method.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why knowing divine attributes is important for key theological beliefs and how Buti structures his explanation.

Core Idea
Divine attributes are the key to understanding human free will and God's decree.

Buti begins by emphasizing that studying divine attributes is not merely theoretical; it directly impacts our understanding of human choice, predestination, and causality. He then outlines his systematic method, which will guide the entire discussion.

Guided Path
1
Read the importance statement
Read the first sentence carefully. Notice how Buti links knowledge of attributes to crucial beliefs about human action and God's decree.
2
Identify the two categories of attributes
Buti will explain two types: attributes of meanings (ṣifāt al-maʿānī) and affective attributes (al-ṣifāt al-maʿnawiyya). Find these in the method outline.
3
Notice the structure
The method involves explaining each attribute's meaning, its proof, and its object. This is the plan for the coming lessons.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إن لمعرفة هذه الصفات بخصوصها أهمية أخرى ، إذ ينبثق من معرفتها ومعرفة ضرورة الإيمان بها حقائق هامة يجب اعتقادها والإيمان بها ، كتلك الحقائق المتعلقة بتسيير الإنسان واختياره وقضاء الله وقدره وأثر العلية وعدمها في أفعاله سبحانه وتعالى
وسنتبع في شرح هذه الصفات الطريقة التالية :
۱ - ذكر صفات المعاني وبيان معنى كل منها ودليله ٢ - ذكر الصفات المعنوية ومعنى كل منها - بيان متعلق هذه الصفات
✩
۱ - ذكر هذه الصفات وبيان معنى كل منها ودليله
۱ - ( العلم ) وهي صفة أزلية قائمة بذاته تعالى يتأتى بها كشف الأمور والإحاطة بها على ما هي عليه في الواقع أو على ما ستكون عليه في المستقبل
·
ولدى تأملك في هذا التعريف تعلم أن هذه الصفة ليس من شأنها تخصيص الممكنات أو التأثير فيها بوجه من الوجوه ، ولكن شأنها مجرد الكشف والاطلاع ، سواء تعلق بواقع ظهر إلى الوجود أم بمغيب لا يزال في جوف العدم . ودليل هذه الصفة آيات كثيرة في كتاب الله تعالى مثل قوله تعالى : ( إنَّ الله بِكُلِّ شيءٍ عَليمٌ } [ التوبة : ١١٥ ]
Then indeed, knowing these attributes specifically has another importance, for from knowing them and knowing the necessity of believing in them emerge important truths that must be believed and have faith in, such as those truths related to human conduct and choice, Allah's decree and predestination, and the effect of causality and its absence in His actions, exalted is He. And we will follow in explaining these attributes the following method: 1. Mention the attributes of meanings (ṣifāt al-maʿānī) and explain the meaning of each and its proof. 2. Mention the affective attributes (al-ṣifāt al-maʿnawiyya) and the meaning of each. - Statement of the objects of these attributes. ✩ 1. Mention of these attributes and explanation of the meaning of each and its proof. 1. (Knowledge - al-ʿIlm): It is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, exalted is He, by which the disclosure and encompassment of matters is obtained, as they are in reality or as they will be in the future. · And upon your reflection on this definition, you know that this attribute does not involve specifying contingent things or influencing them in any way, rather its function is mere disclosure and awareness, whether it pertains to a reality that has appeared into existence or to an unseen that still lies in the depths of non-existence. And the proof of this attribute is many verses in the Book of Allah, such as His saying, exalted: 'Indeed, Allah of all things is Knowing' [Quran 9:115].
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage is an introductory section explaining the importance of knowing the divine attributes and outlining the method the author will follow, then providing the first example: the attribute of knowledge (al-ʿIlm). The author begins by stating that knowing these attributes specifically has a further importance because from it arise crucial truths that must be believed, such as those concerning human free will and divine predestination, causality and its absence in God's actions. Then he declares that in explaining the attributes he will follow this method: first, mention the attributes of meanings (ṣifāt al-maʿānī) and explain each one's meaning and proof; second, mention the affective attributes (al-ṣifāt al-maʿnawiyya) and their meanings; and third, state the objects (mutaʿalliq) of these attributes. After this plan, he begins with the first attribute, knowledge. He defines it as an eternal attribute subsisting in God's essence by which the disclosure and comprehensive knowledge of things is obtained, both as they are in reality and as they will be in the future. He then clarifies a key point: this attribute does not specify or influence contingent things in any way; it is purely for disclosure and awareness, whether the object is present or still non-existent. Finally, he provides the proof from the Quran, citing the verse 'Indeed, Allah of all things is Knowing' (9:115) as an example of the many scriptural evidences.

Key Terms
صفات المعاني
الصفات المعنوية

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The history of Islam
B) Human conduct, choice, and divine decree

D) The rules of fiqh

Key Takeaway
Knowing divine attributes is essential for understanding human free will and God's decree, and Buti will explain them systematically.

?
Buti says that knowing these attributes gives rise to truths about causality in God's actions. Are you willing to stop attributing events in your life to mere chance or secondary causes, and instead see every outcome as directly from Him? What would that shift cost you?

The Attribute of Knowledge: Definition and Proof
Buti defines the attribute of knowledge (al-ʿIlm) and provides its scriptural proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition and exclusive function of God's attribute of knowledge (al-ʿIlm) and its scriptural proof.

Core Idea
God's knowledge is pure awareness, not determination — it discloses reality without influencing it.

Buti now begins his detailed exposition with the first attribute: knowledge (al-ʿIlm). He defines it as an eternal attribute of God that encompasses all things, past and future, and emphasizes that it does not cause or specify objects — it merely discloses them. The Quran provides abundant proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of knowledge
Read the definition carefully. Note that knowledge is described as eternal and subsisting in God's essence, and it results in disclosure and encompassment of matters.
2
Understand the function of knowledge
Buti clarifies that knowledge does not influence or determine objects. It is only for disclosure. This is a key distinction.
3
Review the proof
The proof is from the Quran, specifically the verse 'Indeed, Allah of all things is Knowing.' Understand that this verse affirms comprehensive divine knowledge.

Reason for Discussing the Mu'tazila: Refuting Orientalist Exploitation
Explains why author discusses Mu'tazila view despite having Sunni consensus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the author addresses the Mu'tazila view despite already having the Sunni consensus: it is to counter Orientalist and missionary distortions that aim to create confusion among Muslims.

Core Idea
The author discusses the Mu'tazila not for debate, but to protect Muslims from confusion sown by Orientalists.

In this passage, the author explains a key methodological choice. He could have simply presented the Sunni consensus derived from Quran, Sunnah, and reason. However, he chooses to bring up the Mu'tazila view because Orientalist and missionary circles have intentionally distorted the issue. The author's goal is to expose and refute these distortions, not to engage in pure sectarian polemic.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation to grasp the author's main point.
Pay attention to the phrase 'الكيد الاستشراقي والتبشيري'.
2
Identify the author's main reasoning
The author states that he could have sufficed with the Sunni view. Find the condition that changes this.
Look for 'لولا أن' in the Arabic text.
3
Understand the role of Orientalist scheming
The text mentions 'الكيد الاستشراقي والتبشيري' (Orientalist and missionary scheming). Understand that this is the driving force behind the discussion.
The author uses strong words: 'خوضاً باطلاً عجيباً' to describe their interference.
4
Reflect on the methodological approach
Consider why the author chooses to address a minority view. This teaches us that responding to distortions is necessary even if the mainstream view is sufficient.
This lesson is about the defense of Islamic creed against external attacks.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أنه كان بوسعنا أن نكتفي في هذا الصدد بعرض ما استيقنـه جمهور المسلمين أهل السنة والجماعة ، أخذاً من الكتاب والسنة ، ومقتضيات العقل السليم ، دون أن نعرّج على رأي المعتزلة في ذلك ونذكر أسباب هذا الخلاف . نقول ، كان بوسعنا أن نفعل ذلك ، لولا أن الكيد الاستشراقي والتبشيري خاض في هذه المسألة خوضاً باطلاً عجيباً ، أملاً منه بأن يخلف أي تشويش في ذهن أي فئة أو جماعة من المسلمين بأي شكل من الأشكال
And know that we could have sufficed in this regard by presenting what the majority of Muslims, the People of the Sunnah and the Community, are certain of, taken from the Book and the Sunnah and the dictates of sound reason, without mentioning the opinion of the Mu'tazila on that and mentioning the causes of this disagreement. We say, we could have done that, were it not for the Orientalist and missionary scheming, which delved into this issue with a false and strange delving, hoping to create any confusion in the mind of any group or community of Muslims in any form whatsoever.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This methodological passage explains the author's rationale for discussing the Mu'tazila position. He states that in principle, it would be sufficient to present the Sunni consensus derived from Quran, Sunnah, and reason. However, he must address the Mu'tazila view because Orientalist and missionary circles have exploited this issue, spreading false and strange ideas in order to sow confusion among Muslims. Therefore, the refutation of their distortions requires examining the Mu'tazila stance.

Correction: The author explicitly states that he would have sufficed with the Sunni view; he only discusses the Mu'tazila because Orientalists and missionaries have exploited the issue to spread confusion.

Key Takeaway
The author addresses the Mu'tazila view not as a primary need, but to counter the distortions of Orientalists and missionaries who exploit the issue to confuse Muslims.

Critique of Orientalist and Missionary Methodology
Author critiques unscientific methods of orientalists and missionaries.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the author considers orientalist and missionary scholarship to be unscientific and based on conjecture and bias rather than evidence.

Core Idea
Orientalist 'scholarship' relies on conjecture and grudges, not science.

In this passage, the author launches a sharp critique of the methods used by orientalists and missionaries, particularly when discussing Islamic history and theology. He argues that their claims are not grounded in any scientific methodology, but rather in conjecture, intuition, and personal animosity. To illustrate the absurdity of accepting such 'evidence,' he offers a vivid analogy involving rainclouds and floods.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the strong language: 'أبعد من أن يلحق بها أي دليل'.
2
Identify the main accusation
The author states that orientalist and missionary knowledge is not subject to scientific methods. Identify the method he claims they use instead.
The phrase 'منهج التوسم والحدس والأحقاد' is key.
3
Analyze the analogy
The author gives an example: if he saw black clouds and claimed a flood had occurred, would people believe him? Understand how this analogy undermines the credibility of orientalist claims.
This is a rhetorical device to show the absurdity of accepting conjecture as proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فعلوم المستشرقين والمبشرين ، وخاصة في مثل هذه المسائل ، أبعد من أن يلحق بها أي دليل ، وأعلى من أن تخضع لأي منهج من مناهج البحث العلمي ، اللهم إلا منهج التوسم والحدس والأحقاد فحسب ذلك برهاناً على واقع تاريخي ينبغي أن يُصدق وتقام عليه المبادئ والحقائق . ولست أدري لماذا لا يصدقني الناس إذا سخَّرت أنا أيضاً لنفسي هذا المنهج ، فقلت : إنني أرى غيوماً متلبدة سوداء في جهة الشمال ، ولا بد أنها الآن تصب أمطاراً هائلة هناك تسبب عنها طوفان جرف كثيراً من النفوس أو الممتلكات !
For the knowledge of the orientalists and missionaries, especially in such matters, is too far to be attached to any evidence, and too high to be subject to any method of scientific research, except the method of conjecture, intuition, and grudges. That alone is sufficient as proof of a historical reality that should be believed and upon which principles and truths are established. And I do not know why people would not believe me if I myself employed this method for myself, saying: I see dense black clouds in the direction of the north, and surely they are now pouring down huge rains there, causing a flood that has swept away many souls or properties!
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage is a sharp critique of the methodology employed by orientalists and missionaries in historical research, particularly regarding issues of Islamic theology. The author begins by declaring that their scholarship is far from being considered evidence and cannot be subjected to any rigorous scientific method; at best it follows conjecture, intuition, and rancor. He then mocks their approach with a vivid analogy: if he were to see black clouds in the north and conclude that a flood has occurred, would anyone accept that as proof? The absurdity is clear — similarly, their claims about Muslim scholars being confounded are baseless. The author uses this rhetorical device to demonstrate that such 'evidence' is not worthy of acceptance.

Key Terms
المستشرقين
المبشرين
منهج التوسم والحدس والأحقاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Orientalist and missionary scholarship is objective and scientifically rigorous.
Correction: The author argues that such scholarship, especially on Islamic matters, relies on conjecture, intuition, and grudges, not scientific methods.

Checkpoint

C) Textual criticism

Key Takeaway
The author dismisses orientalist and missionary methodology as unscientific, based on conjecture and bias, using a vivid analogy to show its absurdity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Think of a time when you held a strong opinion about a person or group based on your own intuition or a grudge rather than on solid facts. How did that affect your relationship with them and with the truth? Will you commit to seeking evidence before passing judgment from now on?
?
The author mocks the idea of accepting claims based on seeing a cloud and concluding a flood. In what area of your life—your faith, your relationships, your decisions—are you currently seeing 'clouds' and jumping to conclusions? What concrete step can you take this week to replace conjecture with investigation?

Warning Against Superficial Talk About the Mu'tazila
Buti warns against mindless imitation and justifies his detailed approach.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Buti's methodological warning against mindless imitation of Orientalist claims and the rationale for his detailed treatment of the Mu'tazila dispute.

Core Idea
Intellectual rigour demands independent thought, not blind repetition.

In this passage, Buti sets the stage for his detailed discussion of the Mu'tazila and the issue of the createdness of the Quran. He first points out the alarming trend of some Arab Muslims parroting Orientalist claims without reflection. Then he explains that to protect the reader from being misled, he must thoroughly examine the true nature of the dispute. This lesson captures his methodological approach.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the tone of surprise and urgency.
Buti uses strong language ('strange and laughable') to highlight the seriousness of the issue.
2
Identify the target of criticism
Who is Buti criticizing? Distinguish between the Orientalists and their Muslim imitators.
He mocks those who boastfully repeat nonsense without thinking.
3
Understand the purpose
Why does Buti say he must 'detail the discussion'? The answer is to protect the reader from being deceived.
This is a methodological statement: his detailed analysis serves a protective function.
4
Reflect on the lesson
Consider the broader principle: theological discussions require independent reasoning, not imitation.
This prepares you for the coming detailed analysis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولكن العجيب والمضحك حقاً أن تلتفت حولك فتبصر أناساً من العرب المسلمين يتباهون بنفس ذلك السخف ويدندنون بعين ذلك الهراء في نشوة وطرب بالغين دون أن تبصر أي أثر للتأمل والفكر في شيء من كلامهم أو بحوثهم ! ..، فمن أجل أن لا تنطلي عليك أي شبهة من كلام كثيرين ممن خاضوا في الحديث عن تاريخ المعتزلة وقضية خلق القرآن وعدمه من أجانب مستشرقين أو مقلديهم من المسلمين - اقتضت الضرورة أن نفصل القول في ذكر حقيقة هذا الخلاف وجوهره ، ، وأسبابه .
But what is truly strange and laughable is that you look around and see Arab Muslims boasting with the same nonsense and humming the same drivel in extreme ecstasy and delight, without seeing any trace of reflection and thought in any of their speech or research!.. So that no suspicion from the talk of many who have entered into discussion about the history of the Mu'tazila and the issue of the createdness of the Quran, from foreign orientalists or their imitators among Muslims, may deceive you, necessity required that we detail the discussion in mentioning the reality of this dispute and its essence and causes.

Commentary
This passage is an admonition and methodological warning. Buti first ridicules those who mindlessly repeat Orientalist claims without independent thought. Then he states that to protect the reader from being deceived by such superficial talk, he must provide a detailed exposition of the true nature of the dispute with the Mu'tazila regarding the createdness of the Quran. He sets up the need for this detailed discussion.

Common Ground and the Two Madhabs on Mutashabihat
Buti summarizes the common agreement on tanzih and introduces the two madhabs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the universal Muslim agreement on Allah's transcendence (tanzih) and the two methodological approaches—Salaf and Khalaf—towards ambiguous scriptural texts.

Core Idea
All Muslims agree on tanzih; the two schools differ only in handling ambiguous texts.

This passage from Buti establishes a crucial point in Islamic theology: despite differences in interpretation, all Muslims share a fundamental commitment to Allah's transcendence. The author then outlines the two main approaches—the Salaf's cautious avoidance of detailed interpretation and the Khalaf's later inclination. Understanding this common ground is essential before exploring further divisions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the flow from the consensus on tanzih to the divergence into two madhabs.
2
Identify the common agreement
Find where the author states that all Muslims agree on tanzih. What is the basis for this agreement?
The agreement is rooted in obedience to Allah's command and avoidance of following mutashabih.
3
Understand the two madhabs
Notice that after agreeing, they differed into two schools: the early Salaf and the later Khalaf. The author begins to explain the Salaf's unique position.
4
Examine the Salaf's position
The Salaf do not delve into detailed interpretation. Instead, they affirm what Allah affirms, declare transcendence, and adopt general interpretation (ta'wil ijmali) while consigning detailed knowledge to Allah.
This is often called tafwid.
5
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this distinction matters. It shows that the core belief in tanzih is shared, and the difference is methodological, not doctrinal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبناء على ذلك فقد اتفق المسلمون كلهم ، على تنزيه الله تعالى عما يقتضيه ظاهر تلك النصوص القرآنية ، والأحاديث النبوية ، من الصفات المنافية لكمال الله وألوهيته ، تنفيذاً لأمر الله عز وجل ، وانسجاماً مع تحذيره من اتباع المتشابه والخوض في تأويله مع ترك المحكم الواضح . وبعد أن اتفقوا على ذلك - وهذا هو القدر الذي يجب أن يعتقده المسلم - اختلفوا في موقفهم من النصوص المتشابهة ، إلى مذهبين : أولهما تمسك به السلف المتقدمون ، وثانيها جنح إليه من بعدهم من المتأخرين . ما انفرد به السلف : فمذهب السلف ، هو عدم الخوض في أي تأويل أو تفسير تفصيلي لهذه النصوص ، والاكتفاء بإثبات ما أثبته الله تعالى لذاته ، مع تنزيهه عز وجل عن كل نقص ومشابهة للحوادث ، وسبيل ذلك التأويل الإجمالي لهذه النصوص وتحويل العلم التفصيلي بالمقصود منها إلى علم الله عز وجل
And based on that, all Muslims have agreed upon declaring Allah Most High transcendent above what the apparent meaning of those Quranic texts and prophetic hadiths necessitate of attributes contrary to the perfection of Allah and His divinity, in execution of the command of Allah, Mighty and Majestic, and in harmony with His warning against following the mutashabih and delving into its interpretation while leaving aside the clear muhkam. And after they agreed upon that - and this is the extent to which the Muslim must believe - they differed in their stance toward the mutashabihat texts into two schools: the first was adhered to by the early Salaf, and the second inclined to by those after them among the later scholars (khalaf). What the Salaf uniquely held: The madhhab of the Salaf is not to delve into any detailed interpretation or explanation of these texts, and to be content with affirming what Allah Most High has affirmed for Himself, while declaring Him, Mighty and Majestic, transcendent above every deficiency and resemblance to contingent beings, and the way of that is the general (ijmali) interpretation of these texts and consigning detailed knowledge of what is intended from them to the knowledge of Allah, Mighty and Majestic.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is a summary of the common ground and the divergence between the Salaf and Khalaf regarding mutashabihat. It begins by stating that all Muslims unanimously agree on tanzih (transcendence) - that Allah is free from any attributes implied by the apparent meaning of ambiguous texts that would contradict His perfection and divinity. This agreement is in compliance with Allah's command and warning. Then it notes that after this agreement (which is the essential belief required of every Muslim), they differed into two madhabs: the first is that of the early Salaf, the second that of later scholars (Khalaf). The author then explains what is unique to the Salaf: their position is to avoid any detailed interpretation (tafsir tafsili) of these texts, instead affirming what Allah has affirmed for Himself while declaring Him transcendent, and adopting a general interpretation (ta'wil ijmali) and leaving the detailed knowledge of the intended meaning to Allah.

Key Terms
تنزيه (tanzih)
سلف (salaf)
خلف (khalaf)
تأويل إجمالي (ta'wil ijmali)
تفويض (tafwid)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that Salaf and Khalaf disagreed on the principle of tanzih itself.
Correction: The author clarifies that both groups agreed on tanzih; they only differed in the method of handling mutashabihat.

Checkpoint
What is the unique position of the Salaf regarding mutashabihat according to this passage?
A) They interpret them in detail according to linguistic analysis.
B) They reject them completely as unreliable.
C) They refrain from detailed interpretation and adopt general interpretation while consigning the true meaning to Allah.
D) They take the apparent meaning literally without any qualification.

Key Takeaway
Muslims unanimously affirm Allah's transcendence; their methodological difference lies in how to approach ambiguous texts, not in the principle of tanzih itself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a Quranic verse that seems to attribute human-like qualities to Allah, does your heart immediately seek a detailed intellectual explanation to feel secure, or are you content to affirm its truth and trust Allah's wisdom, leaving the precise meaning to Him? This lesson calls you to examine your reliance on reason.
?
The lesson emphasizes that all Muslims agree on tanzih, yet our communities often focus on differences over these texts. Where in your own life do you prioritize labeling others as 'Salafi' or 'Ash'ari' over embodying the shared belief in Allah's transcendence? What specific step can you take this week to unite on common ground?
?
Reflect: Are there areas of faith where you demand detailed answers from scholars before you can trust, rather than practicing tafwid (consigning knowledge to Allah)? How does the Salaf's contentment with general interpretation challenge your need for certainty?
